<mo>+</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a-b=a+(-1)\,b.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle a-b=a+(-1)\,b.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d73ebc4f6251d8e298abd5e56cc0028a2ed25363" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:19.048ex; height:2.843ex;"/></div>
</p><p>Using the visualization of complex numbers in the complex plane, addition has the following geometric interpretation: the sum of two complex numbers <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">a</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span>, interpreted as points in the complex plane, is the point obtained by building a <a href="/wiki/Parallelogram" title="Parallelogram">parallelogram</a> from the three vertices <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">O</span>, and the points of the arrows labeled <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">a</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span> (provided that they are not on a line). Equivalently, calling these points <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">A</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">B</span>, respectively and the fourth point of the parallelogram <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> the <a href="/wiki/Triangle" title="Triangle">triangles</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">OAB</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">XBA</span> are <a href="/wiki/Congruence_(geometry)" title="Congruence (geometry)">congruent</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multiplication_and_square">Multiplication and square<span class="anchor" id="Multiplication"></span><span class="anchor" id="Square"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Multiplication and square">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The rules of  the <a href="/wiki/Distributive_property" title="Distributive property">distributive property</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commutative_property" title="Commutative property">commutative properties</a> (of addition and multiplication), and the defining property <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i><sup>2</sup> = −1</span> apply to complex numbers. It follows that 
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (x+yi)\,(u+vi)=(xu-yv)+(xv+yu)i.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>i</mi>

<mi>v</mi>

<mi>x</mi>

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (x+yi)\,(u+vi)=(xu-yv)+(xv+yu)i.}</annotation>

</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle (x+yi)\,(u+vi)=(xu-yv)+(xv+yu)i.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b7af9a9eaf702d78bc2d6c5a0161fec088ad49a4" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:42.806ex; height:2.843ex;"/></div>
</p><p>In particular,
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (x+yi)^{2}=x^{2}-y^{2}+2xyi.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reciprocal_and_division">Reciprocal and division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reciprocal and division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Using the conjugation, the <a href="/wiki/Multiplicative_inverse" title="Multiplicative inverse">reciprocal</a> of a nonzero complex number <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i> = <i>x</i> + <i>yi</i></span> can always be broken down to

</p><p>since <i>non-zero</i> implies that <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sup>2</sup> + <i>y</i><sup>2</sup></span> is greater than zero.
</p><p>This can be used to express a division of an arbitrary complex number <span class="texhtml"><i>w</i> = <i>u</i> + <i>vi</i></span> by a non-zero complex number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> as

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multiplication_and_division_in_polar_form">Multiplication and division in polar form</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Multiplication and division in polar form">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Complex_multi.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Complex_multi.svg/220px-Complex_multi.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Complex_multi.svg/330px-Complex_multi.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Complex_multi.svg/440px-Complex_multi.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Complex_multi.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Multiplication of <span class="texhtml">2 + <i>i</i></span> (blue triangle) and <span class="texhtml">3 + <i>i</i></span> (red triangle). The red triangle is rotated to match the vertex of the blue one (the adding of both angles in the terms <i>φ</i><sub>1</sub>+<i>φ</i><sub>2</sub> in the equation) and stretched by the length of the <a href="/wiki/Hypotenuse" title="Hypotenuse">hypotenuse</a> of the blue triangle (the multiplication of both radiuses, as per term <i>r</i><sub>1</sub><i>r</i><sub>2</sub> in the equation).</div></div></div>
<p>Formulas for multiplication, division and exponentiation are simpler in polar form than the corresponding formulas in Cartesian coordinates. Given two complex numbers <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i><sub>1</sub> = <i>r</i><sub>1</sub>(cos <i>φ</i><sub>1</sub> + <i>i</i> sin <i>φ</i><sub>1</sub>)</span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i><sub>2</sub> = <i>r</i><sub>2</sub>(cos <i>φ</i><sub>2</sub> + <i>i</i> sin <i>φ</i><sub>2</sub>)</span>, because of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trigonometric_identities" title="Trigonometric identities">trigonometric identities</a>
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{alignedat}{4}\cos a\cos b&amp;-\sin a\sin b&amp;{}={}&amp;\cos(a+b)\\\cos a\sin b&amp;+\sin a\cos b&amp;{}={}&amp;\sin(a+b).\end{alignedat}}}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle z_{1}z_{2}=r_{1}r_{2}(\cos(\varphi _{1}+\varphi _{2})+i\sin(\varphi _{1}+\varphi _{2})).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a6502c352808cfc910a170a23813f02822e9b758" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:43.625ex; height:2.843ex;"/></div>
In other words, the absolute values are multiplied and the arguments are added to yield the polar form of the product. For example, multiplying by <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i></span> corresponds to a quarter-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turn_(geometry)" title="Turn (geometry)">turn</a> counter-clockwise, which gives back <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i><sup>2</sup> = −1</span>. The picture at the right illustrates the multiplication of
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (2+i)(3+i)=5+5i.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo>+</mo>
<mn>5</mn>
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (2+i)(3+i)=5+5i.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle (2+i)(3+i)=5+5i.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/38aeed692cd66f9df75aebfa019e3d57aeeb56b7" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:22.942ex; height:2.843ex;"/></div>
Since the real and imaginary part of <span class="texhtml">5 + 5<i>i</i></span> are equal, the argument of that number is 45 degrees, or <span class="texhtml"><i>π</i>/4</span> (in <a href="/wiki/Radian" title="Radian">radian</a>). On the other hand, it is also the sum of the angles at the origin of the red and blue triangles are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctan" title="Arctan">arctan</a>(1/3) and arctan(1/2), respectively. Thus, the formula

holds. As the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctan" title="Arctan">arctan</a> function can be approximated highly efficiently, formulas like this – known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machin-like_formulas" title="Machin-like formulas">Machin-like formulas</a> – are used for high-precision approximations of <a href="/wiki/Pi" title="Pi"><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span></a>.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Square_root">Square root</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Square root">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Square_root#Square_roots_of_negative_and_complex_numbers" title="Square root">Square roots of negative and complex numbers</a></div>
<p>The square roots of <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + <i>bi</i></span> (with <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i> ≠ 0</span>) are <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \pm (\gamma +\delta i)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle \delta =(\operatorname {sgn} b){\sqrt {\frac {-a+{\sqrt {a^{2}+b^{2}}}}{2}}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ee539b0e662c41dff571c833f41385f05e2c6c8b" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:29.897ex; height:7.676ex;"/></div>
</p><p>where <span class="texhtml">sgn</span> is the <a href="/wiki/Sign_function" title="Sign function">signum</a> function. This can be seen by squaring <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \pm (\gamma +\delta i)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<semantics>

</mover>

<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {a^{2}+b^{2}}}={\sqrt {z{\overline {z}}}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {a^{2}+b^{2}}}={\sqrt {z{\overline {z}}}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a88fbb46c61d4244904eb29921e3e9eeb26db234" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:17.865ex; height:3.509ex;"/></span> where <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i> = <i>a</i> + <i>bi</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAhlfors19793_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAhlfors19793-54">[46]</a></sup>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exponential_function">Exponential function</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Exponential function">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Exponential_function" title="Exponential function">exponential function</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \exp \colon \mathbb {C} \to \mathbb {C} ;z\mapsto \exp z}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>The value at <span class="texhtml">1</span> of the exponential function is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euler%27s_number" title="Euler's number">Euler's number</a>
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle e=\exp 1=\sum _{n=0}^{\infty }{\frac {1}{n!}}\approx 2.71828.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

If <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> is real, one has 
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \exp z=e^{z}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<a href="/wiki/Analytic_continuation" title="Analytic continuation">Analytic continuation</a> allows extending this equality for every complex value of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span>, and thus to define the complex exponentiation with base <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">e</span> as

</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Functional_equation">Functional equation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Functional equation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The exponential function satisfies the <a href="/wiki/Functional_equation" title="Functional equation">functional equation</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle e^{z+t}=e^{z}e^{t}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>z</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>z</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e^{z+t}=e^{z}e^{t}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle e^{z+t}=e^{z}e^{t}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bbba6af40ccf896b0111e3217888a7aa26347619" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:11.697ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>
This can be proved either by comparing the power series expansion of both members or by applying <a href="/wiki/Analytic_continuation" title="Analytic continuation">analytic continuation</a> from the restriction of the equation to real arguments.
</p>
<h4><span id="Euler.27s_formula"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Euler's_formula">Euler's formula</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Euler's formula">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Euler%27s_formula" title="Euler's formula">Euler's formula</a> states that, for any real number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">y</span>,
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle e^{iy}=\cos y+i\sin y.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>y</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>cos</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>sin</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e^{iy}=\cos y+i\sin y.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle e^{iy}=\cos y+i\sin y.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/19fc9cc8265c6af6779ef07d7a6103be3192f6e0" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:19.527ex; height:3.009ex;"/></div>
</p><p>The functional equation implies thus that, if <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">y</span> are real, one has
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle e^{x+iy}=e^{x}(\cos y+i\sin y)=e^{x}\cos y+ie^{x}\sin y,}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>y</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>cos</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>sin</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mi>cos</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>x</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mi>sin</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e^{x+iy}=e^{x}(\cos y+i\sin y)=e^{x}\cos y+ie^{x}\sin y,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle e^{x+iy}=e^{x}(\cos y+i\sin y)=e^{x}\cos y+ie^{x}\sin y,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bc34ad5c33911c8706c864f9dc2c09d5de130f61" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:46.891ex; height:3.176ex;"/></div>
which is the decomposition of the exponential function into its real and imaginary parts.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Complex_logarithm">Complex logarithm</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Complex logarithm">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the real case, the <a href="/wiki/Natural_logarithm" title="Natural logarithm">natural logarithm</a> can be defined as the <a href="/wiki/Inverse_function" title="Inverse function">inverse</a>
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \ln \colon \mathbb {R} ^{+}\to \mathbb {R} ;x\mapsto \ln x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>:<!-- : --></mo>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>+</mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">→<!-- → --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>;</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">↦<!-- ↦ --></mo>
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \ln \colon \mathbb {R} ^{+}\to \mathbb {R} ;x\mapsto \ln x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \ln \colon \mathbb {R} ^{+}\to \mathbb {R} ;x\mapsto \ln x}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7dd4ef60a8d8dd5a7db33ec3e1380a38912ebb29" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.088ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> of the exponential function. For extending this to the complex domain, one can start from Euler's formula. It implies that, if a complex number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle z\in \mathbb {C} ^{\times }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>z</mi>
<mo>∈<!-- ∈ --></mo>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle z\in \mathbb {C} ^{\times }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle z\in \mathbb {C} ^{\times }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8232b7f77cce8dd9abf7820b72fb032829a6be17" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.118ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is written in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_form" title="Polar form">polar form</a>

with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r,\varphi \in \mathbb {R} ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \ln z=\ln r+i\varphi }" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

as <a href="/wiki/Complex_logarithm" title="Complex logarithm">complex logarithm</a> one has a proper inverse:

</p><p>However, because cosine and sine are periodic functions, the addition of an integer multiple of <span class="texhtml">2<i>π</i></span> to <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">φ</span> does not change <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span>. </p><p>Therefore, if the complex logarithm is not to be defined as a <a href="/wiki/Multivalued_function" title="Multivalued function">multivalued function</a>

one has to use a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branch_cut" title="Branch cut">branch cut</a> and to restrict the <a href="/wiki/Codomain" title="Codomain">codomain</a>, resulting in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bijective" title="Bijective">bijective</a> function

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exponentiation">Exponentiation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Exponentiation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>If <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> &gt; 0</span> is real and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> complex, the exponentiation is defined as 
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x^{z}=e^{z\ln x},}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>z</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>e</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>z</mi>
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>x</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{z}=e^{z\ln x},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle x^{z}=e^{z\ln x},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d3a96b52f00374050e10631f7a4268d5ad3081ae" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.248ex; height:3.009ex;"/></div>
where <span class="texhtml">ln</span> denotes the natural logarithm.
</p><p>It seems natural to extend this formula to complex values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>, but there are some difficulties resulting from the fact that the complex logarithm is not really a function, but a <a href="/wiki/Multivalued_function" title="Multivalued function">multivalued function</a>.
</p><p>It follows that if <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> is as above, and if <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">t</span> is another complex number, then the <i>exponentiation</i> is the multivalued function
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle z^{t}=\left\{e^{t\ln r}\,(\cos(\varphi t+2\pi kt)+i\sin(\varphi t+2\pi kt))\}\mid k\in \mathbb {Z} \right\}}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow>

<mi>t</mi>
<mi>ln</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>r</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>cos</mi>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle z^{t}=\left\{e^{t\ln r}\,(\cos(\varphi t+2\pi kt)+i\sin(\varphi t+2\pi kt))\}\mid k\in \mathbb {Z} \right\}}</annotation>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Integer_and_fractional_exponents">Integer and fractional exponents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Integer and fractional exponents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="400" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg/300px-Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg/450px-Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg/600px-Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geometric representation of the 2nd to 6th roots of a complex number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span>, in polar form <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>re</i><sup><i>iφ</i></sup></span> </span> where <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>r</i> = |<i>z</i> |</span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>φ</i> = arg <i>z</i></span></span>. If <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> is real, <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>φ</i> = 0</span> or <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span></span>. Principal roots are shown in black.</div></div></div>
<p>If, in the preceding formula, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">t</span> is an integer, then the sine and the cosine are independent of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">k</span>. Thus, if the exponent <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> is an integer, then <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span> is well defined, and the exponentiation formula simplifies to <a href="/wiki/De_Moivre%27s_formula" title="De Moivre's formula">de Moivre's formula</a>:
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle z^{n}=(r(\cos \varphi +i\sin \varphi ))^{n}=r^{n}\,(\cos n\varphi +i\sin n\varphi ).}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>z</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>r</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>cos</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>sin</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>r</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>cos</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mi>sin</mi>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mi>φ<!-- φ --></mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle z^{n}=(r(\cos \varphi +i\sin \varphi ))^{n}=r^{n}\,(\cos n\varphi +i\sin n\varphi ).}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle z^{n}=(r(\cos \varphi +i\sin \varphi ))^{n}=r^{n}\,(\cos n\varphi +i\sin n\varphi ).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/34fbe9dbcf9f8e1cd62c732028c3eeee9dc8c304" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:49.914ex; height:2.843ex;"/></div>
</p><p>The <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> <a href="/wiki/Nth_root" title="Nth root"><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th roots</a> of a complex number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> are given by
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle z^{1/n}={\sqrt[{n}]{r}}\left(\cos \left({\frac {\varphi +2k\pi }{n}}\right)+i\sin \left({\frac {\varphi +2k\pi }{n}}\right)\right)}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mroot>

<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle z^{1/n}={\sqrt[{n}]{r}}\left(\cos \left({\frac {\varphi +2k\pi }{n}}\right)+i\sin \left({\frac {\varphi +2k\pi }{n}}\right)\right)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle z^{1/n}={\sqrt[{n}]{r}}\left(\cos \left({\frac {\varphi +2k\pi }{n}}\right)+i\sin \left({\frac {\varphi +2k\pi }{n}}\right)\right)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1cc1b3406644f788c1ac1799d6328118ee66516f" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:48.488ex; height:6.176ex;"/></div>
for <span class="texhtml">0 ≤ <i>k</i> ≤ <i>n</i> − 1</span>. (Here <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{r}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>r</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{r}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{r}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/10eb7386bd8efe4c5b5beafe05848fbd923e1413" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.985ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> is the usual (positive) <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root of the positive real number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">r</span>.) Because sine and cosine are periodic, other integer values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">k</span> do not give other values.
</p><p>While the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root of a positive real number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">r</span> is chosen to be the <i>positive</i> real number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">c</span> satisfying <span class="texhtml"><i>c</i><sup><i>n</i></sup> = <i>r</i></span>, there is no natural way of distinguishing one particular complex <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root of a complex number. Therefore, the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root is a <a href="/wiki/Multivalued_function" title="Multivalued function"><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>-valued function</a> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span>. This implies that, contrary to the case of positive real numbers, one has  
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (z^{n})^{1/n}\neq z,}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msup>
<mi>z</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>≠<!-- ≠ --></mo>
<mi>z</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (z^{n})^{1/n}\neq z,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle (z^{n})^{1/n}\neq z,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a9d36550bd902f4562776d5aa8cd7f4c80941eac" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.814ex; height:3.343ex;"/></div>
since the left-hand side consists of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> values, and the right-hand side is a single value.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">Properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Field_structure">Field structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Field structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> of complex numbers is a <a href="/wiki/Field_(mathematics)" title="Field (mathematics)">field</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEApostol198115–16_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEApostol198115–16-56">[47]</a></sup> Briefly, this means that the following facts hold: first, any two complex numbers can be added and multiplied to yield another complex number. Second, for any complex number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span>, its <a href="/wiki/Additive_inverse" title="Additive inverse">additive inverse</a> <span class="texhtml">–<i>z</i></span> is also a complex number; and third, every nonzero complex number has a <a href="/wiki/Multiplicative_inverse" title="Multiplicative inverse">reciprocal</a> complex number. Moreover, these operations satisfy a number of laws, for example the law of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commutativity" title="Commutativity">commutativity</a> of addition and multiplication for any two complex numbers <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i><sub>1</sub></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i><sub>2</sub></span>:
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}z_{1}+z_{2}&amp;=z_{2}+z_{1},\\z_{1}z_{2}&amp;=z_{2}z_{1}.\end{aligned}}}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt">
<mtr>

<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<mi></mi>

</mtd>
</mtr>
</mtable>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}z_{1}+z_{2}&amp;=z_{2}+z_{1},\\z_{1}z_{2}&amp;=z_{2}z_{1}.\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}z_{1}+z_{2}&amp;=z_{2}+z_{1},\\z_{1}z_{2}&amp;=z_{2}z_{1}.\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ab73d971b53c7c080859403782699fd1bd6e85cf" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:18.719ex; height:5.843ex;"/></div>
These two laws and the other requirements on a field can be proven by the formulas given above, using the fact that the real numbers themselves form a field.
</p><p>Unlike the reals, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is not an <a href="/wiki/Ordered_field" title="Ordered field">ordered field</a>, that is to say, it is not possible to define a relation <span class="texhtml"><i>z</i><sub>1</sub> &lt; <i>z</i><sub>2</sub></span> that is compatible with the addition and multiplication. In fact, in any ordered field, the square of any element is necessarily positive, so <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i><sup>2</sup> = −1</span> precludes the existence of an <a href="/wiki/Total_order" title="Total order">ordering</a> on <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEApostol198125_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEApostol198125-57">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>When the underlying field for a mathematical topic or construct is the field of complex numbers, the topic's name is usually modified to reflect that fact. For example: <a href="/wiki/Complex_analysis" title="Complex analysis">complex analysis</a>, complex <a href="/wiki/Matrix_(mathematics)" title="Matrix (mathematics)">matrix</a>, complex <a href="/wiki/Polynomial" title="Polynomial">polynomial</a>, and complex <a href="/wiki/Lie_algebra" title="Lie algebra">Lie algebra</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solutions_of_polynomial_equations">Solutions of polynomial equations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Solutions of polynomial equations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Given any complex numbers (called <a href="/wiki/Coefficient" title="Coefficient">coefficients</a>) <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i><sub>0</sub>, ..., <i>a</i><sub><i>n</i></sub></span>, the equation
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}z^{n}+\dotsb +a_{1}z+a_{0}=0}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mi>z</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>+</mo>
<mo>⋯<!-- ⋯ --></mo>
<mo>+</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mi>z</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<msub>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a_{n}z^{n}+\dotsb +a_{1}z+a_{0}=0}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle a_{n}z^{n}+\dotsb +a_{1}z+a_{0}=0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cd18e443bc73d8469f68a8a4d62e4abd5a5c162f" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:25.919ex; height:2.676ex;"/></div>
has at least one complex solution <i>z</i>, provided that at least one of the higher coefficients <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i><sub>1</sub>, ..., <i>a</i><sub><i>n</i></sub></span> is nonzero.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bourbaki_1998_loc=§VIII.1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bourbaki_1998_loc=§VIII.1-7">[6]</a></sup> This is the statement of the <i><a href="/wiki/Fundamental_theorem_of_algebra" title="Fundamental theorem of algebra">fundamental theorem of algebra</a></i>, of <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss" title="Carl Friedrich Gauss">Carl Friedrich Gauss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean_le_Rond_d%27Alembert" title="Jean le Rond d'Alembert">Jean le Rond d'Alembert</a>. Because of this fact, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is called an <a href="/wiki/Algebraically_closed_field" title="Algebraically closed field">algebraically closed field</a>. This property does not hold for the <a href="/wiki/Rational_number" title="Rational number">field of rational numbers</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Q</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Q} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c5909f0b54e4718fa24d5fd34d54189d24a66e9a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.808ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> (the polynomial <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sup>2</sup> − 2</span> does not have a rational root, since <a href="/wiki/Square_root_of_2" title="Square root of 2">√2</a> is not a rational number) nor the real numbers <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> (the polynomial <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sup>2</sup> + <i>a</i></span> does not have a real root for <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> &gt; 0</span>, since the square of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is positive for any real number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>).
</p><p>There are various proofs of this theorem, by either analytic methods such as <a href="/wiki/Liouville%27s_theorem_(complex_analysis)" title="Liouville's theorem (complex analysis)">Liouville's theorem</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topological</a> ones such as the <a href="/wiki/Winding_number" title="Winding number">winding number</a>, or a proof combining <a href="/wiki/Galois_theory" title="Galois theory">Galois theory</a> and the fact that any real polynomial of <i>odd</i> degree has at least one real root.
</p><p>Because of this fact, theorems that hold <i>for any algebraically closed field</i> apply to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> For example, any non-empty complex <a href="/wiki/Square_matrix" title="Square matrix">square matrix</a> has at least one (complex) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenvalue" title="Eigenvalue">eigenvalue</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Algebraic_characterization">Algebraic characterization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Algebraic characterization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The field <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> has the following three properties:
</p>
<ul><li>First, it has <a href="/wiki/Characteristic_(algebra)" title="Characteristic (algebra)">characteristic</a> 0. This means that <span class="texhtml">1 + 1 + ⋯ + 1 ≠ 0</span> for any number of summands (all of which equal one).</li>
<li>Second, its <a href="/wiki/Transcendence_degree" title="Transcendence degree">transcendence degree</a> over <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Q</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Q} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c5909f0b54e4718fa24d5fd34d54189d24a66e9a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.808ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_field" title="Prime field">prime field</a> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} ,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} ,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c6ff6a3dc2982018ff20f1d2c927afc74a217be6" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Cardinality_of_the_continuum" title="Cardinality of the continuum">cardinality of the continuum</a>.</li>
<li>Third, it is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algebraically_closed" title="Algebraically closed">algebraically closed</a> (see above).</li></ul>
<p>It can be shown that any field having these properties is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isomorphic" title="Isomorphic">isomorphic</a> (as a field) to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_closure" title="Algebraic closure">algebraic closure</a> of the field <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} _{p}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Q</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} _{p}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} _{p}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/35f44bc6894c682710705f3ea74f33042e0acc3e" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.867ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> of the <a href="/wiki/P-adic_number" title="P-adic number"><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">p</span>-adic number</a> also satisfies these three properties, so these two fields are isomorphic (as fields, but not as topological fields).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[49]</a></sup> Also, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is isomorphic to the field of complex <a href="/wiki/Puiseux_series" title="Puiseux series">Puiseux series</a>. However, specifying an isomorphism requires the <a href="/wiki/Axiom_of_choice" title="Axiom of choice">axiom of choice</a>. Another consequence of this algebraic characterization is that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> contains many proper subfields that are isomorphic to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characterization_as_a_topological_field">Characterization as a topological field</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Characterization as a topological field">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The preceding characterization of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> describes only the algebraic aspects of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> That is to say, the properties of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neighborhood_(topology)" title="Neighborhood (topology)">nearness</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continuity_(topology)" title="Continuity (topology)">continuity</a>, which matter in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_analysis" title="Mathematical analysis">analysis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topology</a>, are not dealt with. The following description of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> as a <a href="/wiki/Topological_ring" title="Topological ring">topological field</a> (that is, a field that is equipped with a <a href="/wiki/Topological_space" title="Topological space">topology</a>, which allows the notion of convergence) does take into account the topological properties. <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> contains a subset <span class="texhtml"><i>P</i></span> (namely the set of positive real numbers) of nonzero elements satisfying the following three conditions:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="texhtml"><i>P</i></span> is closed under addition, multiplication and taking inverses.</li>
<li>If <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">y</span> are distinct elements of <span class="texhtml"><i>P</i></span>, then either <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> − <i>y</i></span> or <span class="texhtml"><i>y</i> − <i>x</i></span> is in <span class="texhtml"><i>P</i></span>.</li>
<li>If <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> is any nonempty subset of <span class="texhtml"><i>P</i></span>, then <span class="texhtml"><i>S</i> + <i>P</i> = <i>x</i> + <i>P</i></span> for some <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span></li></ul>
<p>Moreover, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> has a nontrivial <a href="/wiki/Involution_(mathematics)" title="Involution (mathematics)">involutive</a> <a href="/wiki/Automorphism" title="Automorphism">automorphism</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> ↦ <i>x</i>*</span> (namely the complex conjugation), such that <span class="texhtml"><i>x x</i>*</span> is in <span class="texhtml"><i>P</i></span> for any nonzero <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>
</p><p>Any field <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">F</span> with these properties can be endowed with a topology by taking the sets <span class="texhtml"><i>B</i>(<i>x</i>, <i>p</i>) = { <i>y</i> | <i>p</i> − (<i>y</i> − <i>x</i>)(<i>y</i> − <i>x</i>)* ∈ <i>P</i> } </span> as a <a href="/wiki/Base_(topology)" title="Base (topology)">base</a>, where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> ranges over the field and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">p</span> ranges over <span class="texhtml"><i>P</i></span>. With this topology <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">F</span> is isomorphic as a <i>topological</i> field to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>
</p><p>The only <a href="/wiki/Connected_space" title="Connected space">connected</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Locally_compact" title="Locally compact">locally compact</a> <a href="/wiki/Topological_ring" title="Topological ring">topological fields</a> are <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8f4d5d3ec97eee8b915d3b14d3fb38579ee639d2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.325ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> This gives another characterization of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> as a topological field, since <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> can be distinguished from <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> because the nonzero complex numbers are <a href="/wiki/Connected_space" title="Connected space">connected</a>, while the nonzero real numbers are not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBourbaki1998§VIII.4_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBourbaki1998§VIII.4-59">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_construction">Formal construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Formal construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_as_ordered_pairs">Construction as ordered pairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Construction as ordered pairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_Rowan_Hamilton" title="William Rowan Hamilton">William Rowan Hamilton</a> introduced the approach to define the set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> of complex numbers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[51]</a></sup> as the set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} ^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} ^{2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} ^{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e150115ab9f63023215109595b76686a1ff890fd" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.732ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> of <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Ordered_pair" title="Ordered pair">ordered pairs</a> <span class="texhtml">(<i>a</i>, <i>b</i>)</span></span> of real numbers, in which the following rules for addition and multiplication are imposed:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEApostol198115–16_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEApostol198115–16-56">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p><div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}(a,b)+(c,d)&amp;=(a+c,b+d)\\(a,b)\cdot (c,d)&amp;=(ac-bd,bc+ad).\end{aligned}}}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>It is then just a matter of notation to express <span class="texhtml">(<i>a</i>, <i>b</i>)</span> as <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + <i>bi</i></span>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_as_a_quotient_field">Construction as a quotient field</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Complex_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Construction as a quotient field">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Though this low-level construction does accurately describe the structure of the complex numbers, the following equivalent definition reveals the algebraic nature of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">C</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {C} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb{C} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9add4085095b9b6d28d045fd9c92c2c09f549a7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> more immediately. This characterization relies on the notion of fields and polynomials. A field is a set endowed with addition, subtraction, multiplication and division operations that behave as is familiar from, say, rational numbers. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distributive_law" title="Distributive law">distributive law</a>
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (x+y)z=xz+yz}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mi>z</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mi>z</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mi>z</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (x+y)z=xz+yz}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle (x+y)z=xz+yz}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2403554b5d138ef68108772a7bd573477c6d905f" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.823ex; height:2.843ex;"/></div>
must hold for any three elements <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">y</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> of a field. The set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> of real numbers does form a field. A polynomial <span class="texhtml"><i>p</i>(<i>X</i>)</span> with real <a href="/wiki/Coefficient" title="Coefficient">coefficients</a> is an expression of the form
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a_{n}X^{n}+\dotsb +a_{1}X+a_{0},}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
